<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:VG_Industry" title="Template:VG Industry"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>

<p><b>Video game development</b> is the <a href="/wiki/Software_development" title="Software development">process</a> of creating a <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video game</a>. Development is undertaken by a <a href="/wiki/Video_game_developer" title="Video game developer">game developer</a>, which may range from one person to a large business. Traditional commercial <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PC_games" title="PC games">PC</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Console_games" title="Console games">console</a> games are normally funded by a <a href="/wiki/Video_game_publisher" title="Video game publisher">publisher</a> and take several years to develop. <a href="/wiki/Indie_game" title="Indie game">Indie games</a> can take less time and can be produced cheaply by individuals and small developers. The indie game industry has seen a rise in recent years with the growth of new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Online_distribution" title="Online distribution">online distribution</a> systems and the <a href="/wiki/Mobile_game" title="Mobile game">mobile game</a> market.</p>
<p>The first video games were developed in the 1960s, but required <a href="/wiki/Mainframe_computer" title="Mainframe computer">mainframe computers</a> and were not available to the general public. Commercial game development began in the 1970s with the advent of <a href="/wiki/First_generation_of_video_game_consoles" title="First generation of video game consoles">first-generation video game consoles</a> and home computers. Due to low costs and low capabilities of computers, a lone <a href="/wiki/Game_programmer" title="Game programmer">programmer</a> could develop a full game. However, approaching the 21st century, ever-increasing computer processing power and heightened consumer expectations made it difficult for a single developer to produce a mainstream console or PC game. The average cost of producing a video game slowly rose from <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>1–4 million in 2000 to over $5 million in 2006, then to over $20 million by 2010.</p>
<p>Mainstream PC and console games are generally developed in phases. First, in pre-production, pitches, prototypes, and <a href="/wiki/Game_design_document" title="Game design document">game design documents</a> are written. If the idea is approved and the developer receives funding, a full-scale development begins. This usually involves a team of 20–100 individuals with various responsibilities, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Video_game_designer" title="Video game designer">designers</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Video_game_artist" title="Video game artist">artists</a>, programmers, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Video_game_tester" title="Video game tester">testers</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Game development is the <a href="/wiki/Software_development" title="Software development">software development</a> process by which a <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video game</a> is produced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke20034_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke20034-1">[1]</a></sup> Games are developed as a creative outlet<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke20037_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke20037-2">[2]</a></sup> and to generate profit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200314_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200314-3">[3]</a></sup> Development is normally funded by a <a href="/wiki/Video_game_publisher" title="Video game publisher">publisher</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004239_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004239-4">[4]</a></sup> Well-made games bring profit more readily.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200312_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200312-5">[5]</a></sup> However, it is important to estimate a game's financial requirements,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200317_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200317-6">[6]</a></sup> such as development costs of individual features.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200318.E2.80.9319_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200318.E2.80.9319-7">[7]</a></sup> Failing to provide clear implications of game's expectations may result in exceeding allocated budget.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200317_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200317-6">[6]</a></sup> In fact, the majority of commercial games do not produce profit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke20033_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke20033-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forbes_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200317.E2.80.9318_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200317.E2.80.9318-10">[10]</a></sup> Most developers cannot afford changing development schedule and require estimating their capabilities with available resources before production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200318_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200318-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>The game industry requires innovations, as publishers cannot profit from constant release of repetitive sequels and imitations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201019_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201019-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view"><span title="This statement is possibly biased. (February 2014)">neutrality</span></a> is <a href="/wiki/Talk:Video_game_development" title="Talk:Video game development">disputed</a></i>]</sup> Every year new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independent_game_development" title="Independent game development">independent development</a> companies open and some manage to develop hit titles. Similarly, many developers close down because they cannot find a publishing contract or their production is not profitable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201017_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201017-13">[13]</a></sup> It is difficult to start a new company due to high initial investment required.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201037_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201037-14">[14]</a></sup> Nevertheless, growth of casual and mobile game market has allowed developers with smaller teams to enter the market. Once the companies become financially stable, they may expand to develop larger games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201017_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201017-13">[13]</a></sup> Most developers start small and gradually expand their business.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201037_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201037-14">[14]</a></sup> A developer receiving profit from a successful title may store up a capital to expand and re-factor their company, as well as tolerate more failed deadlines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201018_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201018-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>An average development budget for a multiplatform game is <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>18-28M, with high-profile games often exceeding $40M.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the early era of <a href="/wiki/Home_computer" title="Home computer">home computers</a> and video game consoles in the early 1980s, a single <a href="/wiki/Game_programmer" title="Game programmer">programmer</a> could handle almost all the tasks of developing a game — programming, graphical design, sound effects, etc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdamsRollings200613_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdamsRollings200613-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009xxi_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009xxi-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CPGD_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-CPGD-19">[19]</a></sup> It could take as little as six weeks to develop a game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009xxi_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009xxi-18">[18]</a></sup> However, the high user expectations and requirements<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009xxi_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009xxi-18">[18]</a></sup> of modern commercial games far exceed the capabilities of a single developer and require the splitting of responsibilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak20105_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak20105-20">[20]</a></sup> A team of over a hundred people can be employed full-time for a single project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CPGD_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-CPGD-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Game development, production, or design is a process that starts from an idea or concept.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates20043_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates20043-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdamsRollings200629.E2.80.9330_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdamsRollings200629.E2.80.9330-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200375_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200375-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler20093_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler20093-24">[24]</a></sup> Often the idea is based on a modification of an existing game concept.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates20043_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates20043-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdamsRollings200631.E2.80.9333_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdamsRollings200631.E2.80.9333-25">[25]</a></sup> The game idea may fall within one or several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Game_genre" title="Game genre">genres</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates20046_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates20046-26">[26]</a></sup> Designers often experiment with different combinations of genres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates20046_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates20046-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOxland200425_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOxland200425-27">[27]</a></sup> Game designer usually produces initial game proposal document, that contains the concept, gameplay, feature list, setting and story, target audience, requirements and schedule, staff and budget estimates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates200414.E2.80.9316_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates200414.E2.80.9316-28">[28]</a></sup> Different companies have different formal procedures<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004151_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004151-29">[29]</a></sup> and philosophies<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004151_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004151-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200923_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200923-30">[30]</a></sup> regarding game design and development. There is no standardized development method; however commonalities exist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200923_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200923-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009xxi-xxii_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009xxi-xxii-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>Game development is undertaken by a <a href="/wiki/Video_game_developer" title="Video game developer">game developer</a>—ranging from an individual to a large company. There can be independent or publisher-owned studios.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200925_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200925-32">[32]</a></sup> Independent developers rely on financial support from a <a href="/wiki/Video_game_publisher" title="Video game publisher">game publisher</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler200982_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler200982-33">[33]</a></sup> They usually have to develop a game from concept to prototype without external funding. The formal game proposal is then submitted to publishers, who may finance the game development from several months to years. The publisher would retain exclusive rights to distribute and market the game and would often own the intellectual property rights for the game franchise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200925_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200925-32">[32]</a></sup> Publisher's company may also own the developer's company,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200925_32-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200925-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler200987_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler200987-34">[34]</a></sup> or it may have internal development studio(s). Generally the publisher is the one who owns the game's <a href="/wiki/Intellectual_property" title="Intellectual property">intellectual property</a> rights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forbes_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>All but the smallest developer companies work on several titles at once. This is necessary because of the time taken between shipping a game and receiving royalty payments, which may be between 6 and 18 months. Small companies may structure contracts, ask for advances on royalties, use shareware distribution, employ part-time workers and use other methods to meet payroll demands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200926_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200926-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Console_manufacturer" title="Console manufacturer">Console manufacturers</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a>, have a standard set of technical requirements that a game must conform to in order to be approved. Additionally, the game concept must be approved by the manufacturer, who may refuse to approve certain titles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler200990_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler200990-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most modern PC or console games take from one to three years to complete.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, where as a mobile game can be developed in a few months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MGA_SoA_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-MGA_SoA-37">[37]</a></sup> The length of development is influenced by a number of factors, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Computer_and_video_game_genres" title="Computer and video game genres">genre</a>, scale, development platform and amount of assets.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Some games can take much longer than the average time frame to complete. An infamous example is <a href="/wiki/3D_Realms" title="3D Realms">3D Realms</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/Duke_Nukem_Forever" title="Duke Nukem Forever">Duke Nukem Forever</a></i>, announced to be in production in April 1997 and released fourteen years later in June 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Planning for Maxis' game <i><a href="/wiki/Spore_(2008_video_game)" title="Spore (2008 video game)">Spore</a></i> began in late 1999; the game was released nine years later in September 2008.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The game <i><a href="/wiki/Prey_(2006_video_game)" title="Prey (2006 video game)">Prey</a></i> was briefly profiled in a 1997 issue of PC Gamer, but was not released until 2006, and only then in highly altered form. Finally, <i><a href="/wiki/Team_Fortress_2" title="Team Fortress 2">Team Fortress 2</a></i> was in development from 1998 until its 2007 release, and emerged from a convoluted development process involving "probably three or four different games", according to <a href="/wiki/Gabe_Newell" title="Gabe Newell">Gabe Newell</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>The game revenue from retails is divided among the parties along the distribution chain, such as — developer, publisher, retail, manufacturer and console royalty. Many developers fail to profit from this and go bankrupt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200926_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200926-35">[35]</a></sup> Many developers seek alternative economic models through Internet marketing and distribution channels to improve returns.,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200926.E2.80.9327_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200926.E2.80.9327-40">[40]</a></sup> as through a mobile distribution channel the share of a developer can be up to 70% of the total revenue <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MGA_SoA_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-MGA_SoA-37">[37]</a></sup> and through an online distribution channel almost 100%.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Xgs_pic_ss_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1195" data-file-width="1200" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Xgs_pic_ss_01.jpg/220px-Xgs_pic_ss_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Xgs_pic_ss_01.jpg/330px-Xgs_pic_ss_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Xgs_pic_ss_01.jpg/440px-Xgs_pic_ss_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Xgs_pic_ss_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The XGS PIC 16-Bit game development board, a game development tool<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> similar to those used in the 1990s.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The history of game making begins with the development of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_video_game" title="First video game">first video games</a>, although which video game is the first depends on the definition of <i>video game</i>. The first games created had little entertainment value, and their development focus was separate from user experience—in fact, these games required mainframe computers to play them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak20107_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak20107-42">[42]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/OXO" title="OXO">OXO</a></i>, written by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexander_S._Douglas" title="Alexander S. Douglas">Alexander S. Douglas</a> in 1952, was the first computer game to use a digital display.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak20105_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak20105-20">[20]</a></sup> In 1958, a game called <i><a href="/wiki/Tennis_for_Two" title="Tennis for Two">Tennis for Two</a></i>, which displayed its output on an oscilloscope, was made by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Willy_Higinbotham" title="Willy Higinbotham">Willy Higinbotham</a>, a physicist working at the <a href="/wiki/Brookhaven_National_Laboratory" title="Brookhaven National Laboratory">Brookhaven National Laboratory</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak20106_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak20106-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1983magazine_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-1983magazine-44">[44]</a></sup> In 1961, a mainframe computer game called <i><a href="/wiki/Spacewar!" title="Spacewar!">Spacewar!</a></i> was developed by a group of <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a> students led by <a href="/wiki/Steve_Russell_(computer_scientist)" title="Steve Russell (computer scientist)">Steve Russell</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak20106_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak20106-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>True commercial design and development of games began in the 1970s, when <a href="/wiki/Arcade_game" title="Arcade game">arcade video games</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_video_game_consoles_(first_generation)" title="History of video game consoles (first generation)">first-generation consoles</a> were marketed. In 1971, <i><a href="/wiki/Computer_Space" title="Computer Space">Computer Space</a></i> was the first commercially sold, coin-operated video game. It used a black-and-white <a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">television</a> for its display, and the computer system was made of <a href="/wiki/7400_series" title="7400 series">74 series</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transistor-transistor_logic" title="Transistor-transistor logic">TTL</a> <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">chips</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> In 1972, the first home console system was released called <a href="/wiki/Magnavox_Odyssey" title="Magnavox Odyssey">Magnavox Odyssey</a>, developed by <a href="/wiki/Ralph_H._Baer" title="Ralph H. Baer">Ralph H. Baer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> That same year, <a href="/wiki/Atari,_Inc." title="Atari, Inc.">Atari</a> released <i><a href="/wiki/Pong" title="Pong">Pong</a></i>, an arcade game that increased video game popularity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBS-GameRev-Time_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-PBS-GameRev-Time-47">[47]</a></sup> The commercial success of <i>Pong</i> led other companies to develop <i>Pong</i> clones, spawning the <a href="/wiki/Video_game_industry" title="Video game industry">video game industry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InformIT_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-InformIT-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>Programmers worked within the big companies to produce games for these devices. The industry did not see huge innovation in game design and a large number of consoles had very similar games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak20109_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak20109-49">[49]</a></sup> Many of these early games were often <i>Pong</i> clones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whittaker-122_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Whittaker-122-50">[50]</a></sup> Some games were different, however, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Gun_Fight" title="Gun Fight">Gun Fight</a></i>, which was significant for several reasons:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allgame_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-allgame-51">[51]</a></sup> an early 1975 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Run_and_gun_(video_game)" title="Run and gun (video game)">on-foot</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multi-directional_shooter" title="Multi-directional shooter">multi-directional shooter</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kotaku_gun_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-kotaku_gun-52">[52]</a></sup> which depicted <a href="/wiki/Player_character" title="Player character">game characters</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kohler19_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-kohler19-53">[53]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Video_game_violence" title="Video game violence">game violence</a>, and human-to-human <a href="/wiki/Action_game" title="Action game">combat</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steinberg_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Steinberg-54">[54]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tomohiro_Nishikado" title="Tomohiro Nishikado">Tomohiro Nishikado</a>'s original version was based on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Discrete_logic" title="Discrete logic">discrete logic</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kohler18_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-kohler18-55">[55]</a></sup> which <a href="/wiki/Dave_Nutting" title="Dave Nutting">Dave Nutting</a> adapted using the <a href="/wiki/Intel_8080" title="Intel 8080">Intel 8080</a>, making it the first video game to use a <a href="/wiki/Microprocessor" title="Microprocessor">microprocessor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kent_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kent-56">[56]</a></sup> Console manufacturers soon started to produce consoles that were able to play independently developed games,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201013_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201013-57">[57]</a></sup> and ran on microprocessors, marking the beginning of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_video_game_consoles_(second_generation)" title="History of video game consoles (second generation)">second-generation consoles</a>, beginning with the release of the <a href="/wiki/Fairchild_Channel_F" title="Fairchild Channel F">Fairchild Channel F</a> in 1976.</p>
<p>The flood of <i>Pong</i> clones led to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Video_game_crash_of_1977" title="Video game crash of 1977">video game crash of 1977</a>, which eventually came to an end with the mainstream success of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taito_Corporation" title="Taito Corporation">Taito</a>'s 1978 arcade <a href="/wiki/Shooter_game" title="Shooter game">shooter game</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Space_Invaders" title="Space Invaders">Space Invaders</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whittaker-122_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Whittaker-122-50">[50]</a></sup> marking the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_age_of_arcade_video_games" title="Golden age of arcade video games">golden age of arcade video games</a> and inspiring dozens of manufacturers to enter the market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whittaker-122_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-Whittaker-122-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kent-500_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kent-500-58">[58]</a></sup> Its creator Nishikado not only designed and programmed the game, but also did the artwork, engineered the <a href="/wiki/Video_game_arcade_cabinet" title="Video game arcade cabinet">arcade hardware</a>, and put together a <a href="/wiki/Microcomputer" title="Microcomputer">microcomputer</a> from scratch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1UP-10things_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-1UP-10things-59">[59]</a></sup> It was soon <a href="/wiki/Porting" title="Porting">ported</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Atari_2600" title="Atari 2600">Atari 2600</a>, becoming the first "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Killer_app" title="Killer app">killer app</a>" and quadrupling the console's sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RG-41_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-RG-41-60">[60]</a></sup> At the same time, <a href="/wiki/Home_computer" title="Home computer">home computers</a> appeared on the market, allowing individual programmers and hobbyists to develop games. This allowed hardware manufacturer and software manufacturers to act separately. A very large amount of games could be produced by single individuals, as games were easy to make because graphical and memory limitation did not allow for much content. Larger companies developed, who focused selected teams to work on a title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201012_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201012-61">[61]</a></sup> The developers of many early home video games, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Zork" title="Zork">Zork</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baseball_(computer_game)" title="Baseball (computer game)">Baseball</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Air_Warrior" title="Air Warrior">Air Warrior</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Colossal_Cave_Adventure" title="Colossal Cave Adventure">Adventure</a></i>, later transitioned their work as products of the early video game industry.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<table class="rquote floatright" role="presentation" style="border-collapse:collapse; border-style:none; float:right; margin:0.5em 0.75em; width:33%;">
<tr style="text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">“</td>
<td style="padding:0 10px;">I wouldn't recommend [designing computer games] for someone with a weak heart or a large appetite</td>
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; text-align:right; vertical-align:bottom; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">”</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="rquotecite" colspan="3" style="padding-top:10px; font-size:smaller; line-height:1em; text-align:right;"><cite>— Jon Freeman, 1984<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freeman198412_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-freeman198412-62">[62]</a></sup></cite></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The industry expanded significantly at the time, with the arcade video game sector alone (representing the largest share of the gaming industry) generating higher revenues than both <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop music</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_States" title="Cinema of the United States">Hollywood films</a> combined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogers-Larsen-263_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rogers-Larsen-263-63">[63]</a></sup> The home video game industry, however, suffered major losses following the <a href="/wiki/North_American_video_game_crash_of_1983" title="North American video game crash of 1983">North American video game crash of 1983</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> In 1984 <a href="/wiki/Jon_Freeman" title="Jon Freeman">Jon Freeman</a> warned in <i>Computer Gaming World</i>:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p><i>Q: Are computer games the way to fame and fortune?</i></p>
<p>A: No. Not unless your idea of fame is having your name recognized by one or two astute individuals at <a href="/wiki/Origins_Game_Fair" title="Origins Game Fair">Origins</a> ... I've been making a living (after a fashion) designing games for most of the last six years. I wouldn't recommend it for someone with a weak heart or a large appetite, though.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freeman198412_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-freeman198412-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p><a href="/wiki/Chris_Crawford_(game_designer)" title="Chris Crawford (game designer)">Chris Crawford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Don_Daglow" title="Don Daglow">Don Daglow</a> in 1987 similarly advised prospective designers to write games as a hobby first, and to not quit their existing jobs early.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cgw198702_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-cgw198702-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daglow198709_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-daglow198709-66">[66]</a></sup> The home video game industry was revitalized soon after by the widespread success of the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_Entertainment_System" title="Nintendo Entertainment System">Nintendo Entertainment System</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 1987 a video game required 12 months to develop and another six to plan marketing. Projects remained usually solo efforts, with single developers delivering finished games to their publishers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daglow198709_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-daglow198709-66">[66]</a></sup> With the ever-increasing processing and graphical capabilities of arcade, console and computer products, along with an increase in user expectations, game design moved beyond the scope of a single developer to produce a marketable game in a reasonable time.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This sparked the beginning of team-based development.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In broad terms, during the 1980s, pre-production involved sketches and test routines of the only developer. In the 1990s, pre-production consisted mostly of game art previews. In the early 2000s, pre-production usually produced a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_playable_demo" title="First playable demo">playable demo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200326_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200326-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2000 a 12 to 36 month development project was funded by a publisher for <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>1M–3M.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200315_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200315-69">[69]</a></sup> Additionally, $250k–1.5M were spent on marketing and sales development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200315.E2.80.9316_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200315.E2.80.9316-70">[70]</a></sup> In 2001, over 3000 games were released for PC; and from about 100 games turning profit only about 50 made significant profit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200315_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200315-69">[69]</a></sup> In the early 2000s it became increasingly common to use <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Game_Middleware" title="Game Middleware">middleware game engines</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Quake_engine" title="Quake engine">Quake engine</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unreal_engine" title="Unreal engine">Unreal engine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200330_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200330-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the early 2000s, also <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_games" title="Mobile games">mobile games</a> started to gain popularity. However, mobile games distributed by mobile operators remained a marginal form of gaming until the Apple <a href="/wiki/App_Store_(iOS)" title="App Store (iOS)">App Store</a> was launched in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MGA_SoA_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-MGA_SoA-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2005, a mainstream console video game cost from <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>3M to $6M to develop. Some games cost as much as $20M to develop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> In 2006 the profit from a console game sold at retail was divided among parties of distribution chain as follows: developer (13%), publisher (32%), retail (32%), manufacturer (5%), console royalty (18%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200926_35-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200926-35">[35]</a></sup> In 2008 a developer would retain around 17% of retail price and around 85% if sold online.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forbes_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_video_game_consoles_(third_generation)" title="History of video game consoles (third generation)">third generation of consoles</a>, the home video game industry has constantly increased and expanded. The industry revenue has increased at least five-fold since the 1990s. In 2007, the software portion of video game revenue was $9.5 billion, exceeding that of the movie industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201015_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201015-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Apple App Store, introduced in 2008, was the first mobile application store operated directly by the mobile platform holder. It significantly changed the consumer behaviour more favourable for downloading mobile content and quickly broadened the markets of mobile games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MGA_SoA_37-3"><a href="#cite_note-MGA_SoA-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009 games market annual value was estimated between $7–30 billion, depending on which sales figures are included. This is on par with films box office market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200924_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200924-74">[74]</a></sup> A publisher would typically fund an independent developer for $500k–$5M for a development of a title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200925_32-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200925-32">[32]</a></sup> In 2012, the total value had already reached $66,3 billion and by then the video game markets were not anymore dominated by console games. According to Newzoo, the share of MMO's was 19.8%, PC/MAC's 9.8%, tablets' 3.2%, smartphones 10.6%, handhelds' 9.8%, consoles' only 36.7% and online casual games 10.2%. The fastest growing market segments being mobile games with an average annual rate of 19% for smartphones and 48% for tablets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the past several years, many developers opened and many closed down. Each year a number of developers are acquired by larger companies or merge with existing companies. For example, in 2007 <a href="/wiki/Blizzard_Entertainment" title="Blizzard Entertainment">Blizzard Entertainment</a>'s parent company, <a href="/wiki/Vivendi_Games" title="Vivendi Games">Vivendi Games</a> merged with <a href="/wiki/Activision" title="Activision">Activision</a>. In 2008 <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a> nearly acquired <a href="/wiki/Take-Two_Interactive" title="Take-Two Interactive">Take-Two Interactive</a>. In 2009 <a href="/wiki/Midway_Games" title="Midway Games">Midway Games</a> was acquired by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Time-Warner" title="Time-Warner">Time-Warner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eidos_Interactive" title="Eidos Interactive">Eidos Interactive</a> merged with <a href="/wiki/Square_Enix" title="Square Enix">Square Enix</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201016_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201016-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Roles">Roles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Roles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Q: What lessons had you learned from these ventures which you could share for the benefits of fans wanting to enter the game industry?</p>
<p><br/></p>
A: In the old days, when people asked me what they should study to become a game designer, I suggested literature, art and/or programming. Today, I recommend an undergraduate degree in professional management, followed by an MBA.
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>— <a href="/wiki/Brian_Moriarty" title="Brian Moriarty">Brian Moriarty</a>, 2006<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-acg20060915_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-acg20060915-77">[77]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Producer">Producer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Producer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Video_game_producer" title="Video game producer">Video game producer</a></div>
<p>Development is overseen by internal and external producers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004154_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004154-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201071_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201071-79">[79]</a></sup> The producer working for the developer is known as the <i>internal producer</i> and manages the development team, schedules, reports progress, hires and assigns staff, and so on.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201071_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201071-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004156.E2.80.93158_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004156.E2.80.93158-80">[80]</a></sup> The producer working for the publisher is known as the <i>external producer</i> and oversees developer progress and budget.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004154.E2.80.93156_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004154.E2.80.93156-81">[81]</a></sup> Producer's responsibilities include <a href="/wiki/Public_relations" title="Public relations">PR</a>, contract negotiation, liaising between the staff and stakeholders, schedule and budget maintenance, <a href="/wiki/Quality_assurance" title="Quality assurance">quality assurance</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Betaware" title="Betaware">beta</a> test management, and localization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201071_79-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201071-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004153_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004153-82">[82]</a></sup> This role may also be referred to as <i>project manager</i>, <i>project lead</i>, or <i>director</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201071_79-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201071-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004153_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004153-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Publisher">Publisher</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Publisher">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Video_game_publisher" title="Video game publisher">Video game publisher</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(April 2010)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A video game publisher is a company that publishes video games that they have either developed internally or have had developed by an external video game developer. As with book publishers or publishers of DVD movies, video game publishers are responsible for their product's manufacturing and marketing, including market research and all aspects of advertising.</p>
<p>They usually finance the development, sometimes by paying a video game developer (the publisher calls this external development) and sometimes by paying an internal staff of developers called a studio. Consequently, they also typically own the IP of the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MGA_SoA_37-4"><a href="#cite_note-MGA_SoA-37">[37]</a></sup> Large video game publishers also distribute the games they publish, while some smaller publishers instead hire distribution companies (or larger video game publishers) to distribute the games they publish.</p>
<p>Other functions usually performed by the publisher include deciding on and paying for any license that the game may utilize; paying for localization; layout, printing, and possibly the writing of the user manual; and the creation of graphic design elements such as the box design.</p>
<p>Large publishers may also attempt to boost efficiency across all internal and external development teams by providing services such as sound design and code packages for commonly needed functionality.</p>
<p>Because the publisher usually finances development, it usually tries to manage development risk with a staff of producers or project managers to monitor the progress of the developer, critique ongoing development, and assist as necessary. Most video games created by an external video game developer are paid for with periodic advances on royalties. These advances are paid when the developer reaches certain stages of development, called milestones.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Independent_video_game_development" title="Independent video game development">Independent video game developers</a> create games without a publisher and may choose to digitally distribute their games.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_team">Development team</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Development team">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Developers can range in size from small groups making casual games to housing hundreds of employees and producing several large titles. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201037_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201037-14">[14]</a></sup> Companies divide their subtasks of game's development. Individual job titles may vary; however, roles are the same within the industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004151_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004151-29">[29]</a></sup> The development team consists of several members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak20105_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak20105-20">[20]</a></sup> Some members of the team may handle more than one role; similarly more than one task may be handled by the same member.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004151_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004151-29">[29]</a></sup> Team size can vary from 20 to 100 or more members, depending on the game's scope. The most represented are artists, followed by programmers, then designers, and finally, audio specialists, with two to three producers in management. These positions are employed full-time. Other positions, such as testers, may be employed only part-time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201025_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201025-83">[83]</a></sup> Salaries for these positions vary depending on both the experience and the location of the employee. An entry-level programmer can make, on average, around $70,000 annually and an experienced programmer can make, on average, around $125,000 annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>A development team includes these roles or disciplines:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004151_29-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004151-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Designer">Designer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Designer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Video_game_design" title="Video game design">Video game design</a></div>
<p>A game designer is a person who designs <a href="/wiki/Gameplay" title="Gameplay">gameplay</a>, conceiving and designing the rules and structure of a <a href="/wiki/Game" title="Game">game</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESalenZimmerman2003_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESalenZimmerman2003-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOxland2004292_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOxland2004292-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201074_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201074-87">[87]</a></sup> Development teams usually have a lead designer who coordinates the work of other designers. They are the main visionary of the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOxland2004292.E2.80.93296_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOxland2004292.E2.80.93296-88">[88]</a></sup> One of the roles of a designer is being a writer, often employed part-time to conceive game's <a href="/wiki/Narrative" title="Narrative">narrative</a>, dialogue, commentary, <a href="/wiki/Cutscene" title="Cutscene">cutscene</a> narrative, journals, <a href="/wiki/Video_game_packaging" title="Video game packaging">video game packaging</a> content, hint system, etc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004163_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004163-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrathwaiteSchreiber2009171_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrathwaiteSchreiber2009171-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201094_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201094-91">[91]</a></sup> In larger projects, there are often separate designers for various parts of the game, such as, <a href="/wiki/Game_mechanics" title="Game mechanics">game mechanics</a>, <a href="/wiki/User_interface" title="User interface">user interface</a>, <a href="/wiki/Character_(arts)" title="Character (arts)">characters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dialogue" title="Dialogue">dialogue</a>, etc.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Artist">Artist</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Artist">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Game_art_design" title="Game art design">Game art design</a></div>
<p>A game artist is a <a href="/wiki/Visual_arts" title="Visual arts">visual artist</a> who creates video game art.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004171_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004171-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201085_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201085-93">[93]</a></sup> The art production is usually overseen by an <i>art director</i> or <i>art lead</i>, making sure their vision is followed. The art director manages the art team, scheduling and coordinating within the development team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004171_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004171-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>The artist's job may be <a href="/wiki/2D_computer_graphics" title="2D computer graphics">2D</a> oriented or <a href="/wiki/3D_computer_graphics" title="3D computer graphics">3D</a> oriented. <i>2D artists</i> may produce concept art,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201086_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201086-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004173_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004173-95">[95]</a></sup> sprites,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201087_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201087-96">[96]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Texture_(visual_arts)" title="Texture (visual arts)">textures</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201088_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201088-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004176_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004176-98">[98]</a></sup> environmental backdrops or terrain images,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201086_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201086-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004176_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004176-98">[98]</a></sup> and user interface.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201087_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201087-96">[96]</a></sup> <i>3D artists</i> may produce models or <a href="/wiki/Polygon_mesh" title="Polygon mesh">meshes</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201089_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201089-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004175_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004175-100">[100]</a></sup> animation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201089_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201089-99">[99]</a></sup> 3D environment,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201090_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201090-101">[101]</a></sup> and cinematics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201090_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201090-101">[101]</a></sup> Artists sometimes occupy both roles.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Programmer">Programmer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Programmer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Game_programmer" title="Game programmer">Game programmer</a></div>
<p>A game programmer is a <a href="/wiki/Software_engineer" title="Software engineer">software engineer</a> who primarily develops video games or related software (such as <a href="/wiki/Game_development_tool" title="Game development tool">game development tools</a>). The game's <a href="/wiki/Codebase" title="Codebase">codebase</a> development is handled by programmers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004168_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004168-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201078_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201078-103">[103]</a></sup> There are usually one to several <a href="/wiki/Lead_programmer" title="Lead programmer">lead programmers</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004165_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004165-104">[104]</a></sup> who implement the game's starting codebase and overview future development and programmer allocation on individual modules.</p>
<p>Individual programming disciplines roles include:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004168_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004168-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Physics – the programming of the <a href="/wiki/Game_engine" title="Game engine">game engine</a>, including simulating physics, collision, object movement, etc.;</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Game_artificial_intelligence" title="Game artificial intelligence">AI</a> – producing computer agents using game AI techniques, such as scripting, planning, rule-based decisions, etc.</li>
<li>Graphics – the managing of graphical content utilization and memory considerations; the production of graphics engine, integration of <a href="/wiki/3D_modeling" title="3D modeling">models</a>, textures to work along the physics engine.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sound" title="Sound">Sound</a> – integration of music, speech, effect sounds into the proper locations and times.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gameplay" title="Gameplay">Gameplay</a> – implementation of various games rules and features (sometimes called a <i>generalist</i>);</li>
<li>Scripting – development and maintenance of high-level command system for various in-game tasks, such as AI, level editor triggers, etc.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/User_interface" title="User interface">UI</a> – production of user interface elements, like option menus, <a href="/wiki/HUD_(video_gaming)" title="HUD (video gaming)">HUDs</a>, help and feedback systems, etc.</li>
<li>Input processing – processing and compatibility correlation of various input devices, such as keyboard, mouse, gamepad, etc.</li>
<li>Network communications – the managing of data inputs and outputs for local and internet gameplay.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Game_development_tool" title="Game development tool">Game tools</a> – the production of tools to accompany the development of the game, especially for designers and scripters.</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Level_designer">Level designer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Level designer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Level_design" title="Level design">Level design</a></div>
<p>A level designer is a person who creates <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Level_(computer_and_video_games)" title="Level (computer and video games)">levels</a>, challenges or missions for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Computer_game" title="Computer game">computer</a> and/or video games using a specific set of <a href="/wiki/Computer_program" title="Computer program">programs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004162_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004162-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201076_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201076-106">[106]</a></sup> These programs may be commonly available commercial <a href="/wiki/3D_computer_graphics" title="3D computer graphics">3D</a> or <a href="/wiki/2D_computer_graphics" title="2D computer graphics">2D</a> design programs, or specially designed and tailored <a href="/wiki/Level_editor" title="Level editor">level editors</a> made for a specific game.</p>
<p>Level designers work with both incomplete and complete versions of the game. Game programmers usually produce level editors and design tools for the designers to use. This eliminates the need for designers to access or modify game code. Level editors may involve custom <a href="/wiki/High-level_programming_language" title="High-level programming language">high-level</a> <a href="/wiki/Scripting_language" title="Scripting language">scripting languages</a> for interactive environments or AIs. As opposed to the level editing tools sometimes available to the community, level designers often work with placeholders and prototypes aiming for consistency and clear layout before required artwork is completed.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sound_engineer">Sound engineer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Sound engineer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Sound engineers are technical professionals responsible for <a href="/wiki/Sound_effect" title="Sound effect">sound effects</a> and sound positioning. They sometimes oversee <a href="/wiki/Voice_acting" title="Voice acting">voice acting</a> and other sound asset creation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004185.2C_188.2C_191_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004185.2C_188.2C_191-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201091_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201091-108">[108]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Composer" title="Composer">Composers</a> who create a game's <a href="/wiki/Video_game_music" title="Video game music">musical score</a> also comprise a game's sound team, though often this work is outsourced.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tester">Tester</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Tester">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Game_testing" title="Game testing">Game testing</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Quality_assurance" title="Quality assurance">quality assurance</a> is carried out by game testers. A game tester analyzes <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video games</a> to document <a href="/wiki/Software_bug" title="Software bug">software defects</a> as part of a <a href="/wiki/Quality_control" title="Quality control">quality control</a>. Testing is a highly technical field requiring <a href="/wiki/Computing" title="Computing">computing</a> expertise, and analytic competence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004176_98-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004176-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201095_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201095-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>The testers ensure that the game falls within the proposed design: it both works and is entertaining.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004177_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004177-110">[110]</a></sup>This involves testing of all features, compatibility, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Game_localization" title="Game localization">localization</a>, etc. Although, necessary throughout the whole development process, testing is expensive and is often actively utilized only towards the completion of the project.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_process">Development process</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Development process">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Game development is a software development process, as a video game is software with art, audio, and gameplay. Formal software development methods are often overlooked.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke20034_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke20034-1">[1]</a></sup> Games with poor development methodology are likely to run over budget and time estimates, as well as contain a large number of bugs. Planning is important for individual<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke20033_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke20033-8">[8]</a></sup> and group projects alike.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200315_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200315-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>Overall game development is not suited for typical <a href="/wiki/Software_release_life_cycle" title="Software release life cycle">software life cycle</a> methods, such as the <a href="/wiki/Waterfall_model" title="Waterfall model">waterfall model</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004225_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004225-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>One method employed for game development is <a href="/wiki/Agile_software_development" title="Agile software development">agile development</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004218.E2.80.93219_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004218.E2.80.93219-112">[112]</a></sup> It is based on <a href="/wiki/Iterative_design" title="Iterative design">iterative prototyping</a>, a subset of <a href="/wiki/Software_prototyping" title="Software prototyping">software prototyping</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004226.E2.80.93227_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004226.E2.80.93227-113">[113]</a></sup> Agile development depends on feedback and refinement of game's iterations with gradually increasing feature set.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler200947_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler200947-114">[114]</a></sup> This method is effective because most projects do not start with a clear requirement outline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004218.E2.80.93219_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004218.E2.80.93219-112">[112]</a></sup> A popular method of agile software development is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scrum_(development)" title="Scrum (development)">Scrum</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler200941_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler200941-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another successful method is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Personal_Software_Process" title="Personal Software Process">Personal Software Process</a> (PSP) requiring additional training for staff to increase awareness of project's planning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler200941.2C_43.E2.80.9344_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler200941.2C_43.E2.80.9344-116">[116]</a></sup> This method is more expensive and requires commitment of team members. PSP can be extended to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Team_Software_Process" title="Team Software Process">Team Software Process</a>, where the whole team is self-directing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler200944_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler200944-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>Game development usually involves an overlap of these methods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004225_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004225-111">[111]</a></sup> For example, asset creation may be done via waterfall model, because requirements and specification are clear, <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004227_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004227-118">[118]</a></sup> but gameplay design might be done using iterative prototyping.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004227_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004227-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>Development of a commercial game usually includes the following stages:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004203_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004203-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-production">Pre-production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Pre-production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Pre-production</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004204_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004204-121">[121]</a></sup> or <i>design phase</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200326_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200326-68">[68]</a></sup> is a planning phase of the project focused on idea and concept development and production of initial design documents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004203_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004203-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdamsRollings200629_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdamsRollings200629-122">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOxland2004251_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOxland2004251-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler20095.E2.80.939_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler20095.E2.80.939-124">[124]</a></sup> The goal of concept development is to produce clear and easy to understand documentation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004203_120-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004203-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler20096_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler20096-125">[125]</a></sup> which describes all the tasks, schedules and estimates for the development team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003102_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003102-126">[126]</a></sup> The suite of documents produced in this phase is called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Production_plan" title="Production plan">production plan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003101.E2.80.93102_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003101.E2.80.93102-127">[127]</a></sup> This phase is usually not funded by a publisher,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004203_120-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004203-120">[120]</a></sup> however good publishers may require developers to produce plans during pre-production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003102_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003102-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>The concept documentation can be separated into three stages or documents—high concept, pitch and concept;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004203.E2.80.93207_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004203.E2.80.93207-128">[128]</a></sup> however, there is no industry standard naming convention, for example, both Bethke (2003) and Bates (2004) refer to <i>pitch document</i> as "game proposal",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004204_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004204-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003102_126-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003102-126">[126]</a></sup> yet Moore, Novak (2010) refers to <i>concept document</i> as "game proposal".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070_119-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>The late stage of pre-production may also be referred to as <i>proof of concept</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004204_121-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004204-121">[121]</a></sup> or <i>technical review</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070_119-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070-119">[119]</a></sup> when more detailed game documents are produced.</p>
<p>Publishers have started to expect broader game proposals even featuring playable prototypes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003103_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003103-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="High_concept">High concept</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: High concept">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i>High concept</i> is a brief description of a game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070_119-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004204_121-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004204-121">[121]</a></sup> The high concept is the one-or two-sentence response to the question, "What is your game about?".</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pitch">Pitch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Pitch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A <i>pitch</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070_119-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004204_121-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004204-121">[121]</a></sup> <i>concept document</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070_119-6"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070-119">[119]</a></sup> proposal document,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003102_126-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003102-126">[126]</a></sup> or <i>game proposal</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004204_121-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004204-121">[121]</a></sup> is a short summary document intended to present the game's selling points and detail why the game would be profitable to develop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070_119-7"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004204_121-6"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004204-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>Verbal pitches may be made to management within the developer company, and then presented to publishers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004274_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004274-130">[130]</a></sup> A written document may need to be shown to publishers before funding is approved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003102_126-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003102-126">[126]</a></sup> A game proposal may undergo one to several <i>green-light meetings</i> with publisher executives who determine if the game is to be developed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200327_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200327-131">[131]</a></sup> The presentation of the project is often given by the game designers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Game_demo" title="Game demo">Demos</a> may be created for the pitch; however may be unnecessary for established developers with good track records.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>If the developer acts as its own publisher, or both companies are subsidiaries of a single company, then only the upper management needs to give approval.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Concept">Concept</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Concept">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i>Concept document</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004204_121-7"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004204-121">[121]</a></sup> <i>game proposal</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070_119-8"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070-119">[119]</a></sup> or <i>game plan</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler20098_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler20098-132">[132]</a></sup> is a more detailed document than the pitch document.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070_119-9"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201070-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004204_121-8"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004204-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler20096_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler20096-125">[125]</a></sup> This includes all the information produced about the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler20098_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler20098-132">[132]</a></sup> This includes the high concept, game's genre, gameplay description, features, setting, story, target audience, hardware platforms, estimated schedule, marketing analysis, team requirements, and risk analysis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004204.E2.80.93205_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004204.E2.80.93205-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before an approved design is completed, a skeleton crew of programmers and artists usually begins work.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Programmers may develop <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Quick-and-dirty&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Quick-and-dirty (page does not exist)">quick-and-dirty</a> prototypes showcasing one or more features that stakeholders would like to see incorporated in the final product.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Artists may develop concept art and asset sketches as a springboard for developing real game assets.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Producers may work part-time on the game at this point, scaling up for full-time commitment as development progresses.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources.
