(April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Game producers work during pre-production is related to planning the schedule, budget and estimating tasks with the team.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The producer aims to create a solid production plan so that no delays are experienced at the start of the production.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_design_document">Game design document</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Game design document">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Game_design_document" title="Game design document">Game design document</a></div>
<p>Before a full-scale production can begin, the development team produces the first version of a <a href="/wiki/Game_design_document" title="Game design document">game design document</a> incorporating all or most of the material from the initial pitch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004276_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004276-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOxland2004240.2C_274_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOxland2004240.2C_274-135">[135]</a></sup> The design document describes the game's concept and major gameplay elements in detail. It may also include preliminary sketches of various aspects of the game. Design document is sometimes accompanied by functional <a href="/wiki/Software_prototyping" title="Software prototyping">prototypes</a> of some sections of the game.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Design document remains a <a href="/wiki/Living_document" title="Living document">living document</a> throughout the development—often changed weekly or even daily.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOxland2004241_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOxland2004241-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>Compiling a list of game's needs is called "requirement capture".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke20033_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke20033-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Prototype">Prototype</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Prototype">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_for_Mandicor_0.0.5.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Battle_for_Mandicor_0.0.5.png/220px-Battle_for_Mandicor_0.0.5.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Battle_for_Mandicor_0.0.5.png/330px-Battle_for_Mandicor_0.0.5.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Battle_for_Mandicor_0.0.5.png/440px-Battle_for_Mandicor_0.0.5.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_for_Mandicor_0.0.5.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Placeholder graphics are characteristic of early game prototypes.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Writing <a href="/wiki/Software_prototyping" title="Software prototyping">prototypes</a> of gameplay ideas and features is an important activity that allows programmers and game designers to experiment with different <a href="/wiki/Algorithm" title="Algorithm">algorithms</a> and usability scenarios for a game. A great deal of prototyping may take place during <a href="/wiki/Pre-production" title="Pre-production">pre-production</a> before the design document is complete and may, in fact, help determine what features the design specifies. When this happens the prototype is made physical and not on a computer<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, this is so it is easier to test and make changes before wasting time and resources into what could be a canceled idea or project. Prototyping may also take place during active development to test new ideas as the game emerges.</p>
<p>Prototypes are often meant only to act as a <a href="/wiki/Proof_of_concept" title="Proof of concept">proof of concept</a> or to test ideas, by adding, modifying or removing some of the features.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrathwaiteSchreiber2009189_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrathwaiteSchreiber2009189-137">[137]</a></sup> Most algorithms and features debuted in a prototype may be <a href="/wiki/Porting" title="Porting">ported</a> to the game once they have been completed.</p>
<p>Often prototypes need to be developed quickly with very little time for up-front design (around 15 to 20 minutes of testing)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. Therefore, usually very prolific programmers are called upon to quickly code these <a href="/wiki/Testbed" title="Testbed">testbed</a> tools. <a href="/wiki/Rapid_application_development" title="Rapid application development">RAD</a> tools may be used to aid in the quick development of these programs. In case the prototype it is in a physical form, programmers and designers alike will make the game with paper, dice, and other easy to access tools in order to make the prototype faster.</p>
<p>A successful development model is <a href="/wiki/Iterative_design" title="Iterative design">iterative prototyping</a>, where design is refined based on current progress. There are various technology available for video game development<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004226_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004226-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Production is the main stage of development, when assets and <a href="/wiki/Source_code" title="Source code">source code</a> for the game are produced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler20099_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler20099-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mainstream production is usually defined as the period of time when the project is fully staffed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Programmers write new <a href="/wiki/Source_code" title="Source code">source code</a>, artists develop game assets, such as, <a href="/wiki/Sprite_(computer_graphics)" title="Sprite (computer graphics)">sprites</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3D_model" title="3D model">3D models</a>. Sound engineers develop sound effects and composers develop music for the game. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Level_designer" title="Level designer">Level designers</a> create levels, and writers write dialogue for cutscenes and <a href="/wiki/Non-player_character" title="Non-player character">NPCs</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (April 2010)">original research?</span></a></i>]</sup> Game designers continue to develop the game's design throughout production.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Design">Design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Game_design" title="Game design">Game design</a></div>
<p>Game design is an essential and collaborative<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004xxi_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004xxi-140">[140]</a></sup> process of designing the content and rules of a <a href="/wiki/Game" title="Game">game</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrathwaiteSchreiber20092_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrathwaiteSchreiber20092-141">[141]</a></sup> requiring artistic and technical competence as well as writing skills.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdamsRollings200620.2C_22.E2.80.9323.2C_24.E2.80.9325_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdamsRollings200620.2C_22.E2.80.9323.2C_24.E2.80.9325-142">[142]</a></sup> Creativity and an open mind is vital for the completion of a successful video game.</p>
<p>During development, the game designer implements and modifies the game design to reflect the current vision of the game. Features and levels are often removed or added. The art treatment may evolve and the backstory may change. A new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Platform_(computing)" title="Platform (computing)">platform</a> may be targeted as well as a new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demographic" title="Demographic">demographic</a>. All these changes need to be documented and disseminated to the rest of the team. Most changes occur as updates to the design document.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Programming">Programming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Programming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Game_programming" title="Game programming">Game programming</a></div>
<p>The programming of the game is handled by one or more <a href="/wiki/Game_programmer" title="Game programmer">game programmers</a>. They develop prototypes to test ideas, many of which may never make it into the final game. The programmers incorporate new features demanded by the game design and fix any bugs introduced during the development process. Even if an off-the-shelf <a href="/wiki/Game_engine" title="Game engine">game engine</a> is used, a great deal of programming is required to customize almost every game.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Level_creation">Level creation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Level creation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Level_design" title="Level design">Level design</a></div>
<p>From a time standpoint, the game's first level takes the longest to develop. As level designers and artists use the tools for level building, they request features and changes to the in-house tools that allow for quicker and higher quality development. Newly introduced features may cause old levels to become obsolete, so the levels developed early on may be repeatedly developed and discarded. Because of the dynamic environment of game development, the design of early levels may also change over time. It is not uncommon to spend upwards of twelve months on one level of a game developed over the course of three years. Later levels can be developed much more quickly as the feature set is more complete and the game vision is clearer and more stable.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_production">Art production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Art production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Game_art_design" title="Game art design">Game art design</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>

</tr>
</table>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Audio_production">Audio production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Audio production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Game audio may be separated into three categories—sound effects, music, and voice-over.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200349_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200349-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sound effect production is the production of sounds by either tweaking a sample to a desired effect or replicating it with real objects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200349_143-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200349-143">[143]</a></sup> Sound effects are important and impact the game's delivery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003363_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003363-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>Music may be synthesized or performed live.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200350_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200350-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are several ways in which music is presented in a game.</p>
<ul>
<li>Music may be ambient, especially for slow periods of game, where the music aims to reinforce the aesthetic mood and game setting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003344_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003344-146">[146]</a></sup></li>
<li>Music may be triggered by in-game events. For example, in such games as <a href="/wiki/Pac-Man" title="Pac-Man">Pac-Man</a> or <a href="/wiki/Mario" title="Mario">Mario</a>, player picking up <a href="/wiki/Power-up" title="Power-up">power-ups</a> triggered respective musical scores.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003344_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003344-146">[146]</a></sup></li>
<li>Action music, such as chase, battle or hunting sequences is fast-paced, hard-changing score.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003345_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003345-147">[147]</a></sup></li>
<li>Menu music, similar to credits music, creates aural impact while relatively little action is taking place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003345_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003345-147">[147]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>A game title with 20 hours of single-player gameplay may feature around 60 minutes of music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003345_147-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003345-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>Voice-overs and voice acting creates character gameplay interactivity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200349_143-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200349-143">[143]</a></sup> Voice acting adds personality to the game's characters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003353_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003353-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Testing">Testing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Testing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Game_testing" title="Game testing">Game testing</a></div>
<p>At the end<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (April 2010)">original research?</span></a></i>]</sup> of the project, <a href="/wiki/Quality_assurance" title="Quality assurance">quality assurance</a> plays a significant role. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Game_tester" title="Game tester">Testers</a> start work once anything is playable. This may be one level or subset of the game software that can be used to any reasonable extent. Early on, testing a game occupies a relatively small amount of time. Testers may work on several games at once. As development draws to a close, a single game usually employs many testers full-time (and often with overtime). They strive to test new features and regression test existing ones. Testing is vital for modern, complex games as single changes may lead to catastrophic consequences.</p>
<p>At this time features and levels are being finished at the highest rate and there is more new material to be tested than during any other time in the project. Testers need to carry out <a href="/wiki/Regression_testing" title="Regression testing">regression testing</a> to make sure that features that have been in place for months still operate correctly. Regression testing is one of the vital tasks required for effective software development. As new features are added, subtle changes to the <a href="/wiki/Codebase" title="Codebase">codebase</a> can produce unexpected changes in different portions of the game. This task is often overlooked, for several reasons. Sometimes, when a feature is implemented and tested, it is considered "working" for the rest of the project and little attention is given to repeated testing. Also, features that are added late in development are prioritized and existing features often receive insufficient testing time. Proper regression testing is also increasingly expensive as the number of features increases and is often not scheduled correctly.</p>
<p>Despite the dangers of overlooking regression testing, some game developers and publishers fail to test the full feature suite of the game and ship a game with bugs. This can result in customers dissatisfaction and failure to meet sales goals. When this does happen, most developers and publishers quickly release <a href="/wiki/Patch_(computing)" title="Patch (computing)">patches</a> that fix the bugs and make the game fully playable again.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Milestones">Milestones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Milestones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Commercial game development projects may be required to meet milestones set by publisher. Milestones mark major events during game development and are used to track game's progress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009244_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009244-149">[149]</a></sup> Such milestones may be, for example, <i>first playable</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003293_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003293-150">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009244.E2.80.93245_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009244.E2.80.93245-151">[151]</a></sup> <i>alpha</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003294_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003294-152">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245-153">[153]</a></sup> or <i>beta</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245-153">[153]</a></sup> game versions. Project milestones depend on the developer schedules.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009244_149-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009244-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>There is no industry standard for defining milestones, and such vary depending on publisher, year, or project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003192_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003192-154">[154]</a></sup> Some common milestones for two-year development cycle are as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009244_149-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009244-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="First_playable">First playable</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: First playable">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <i>first playable</i> is the game version containing representative gameplay and assets,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009244_149-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009244-149">[149]</a></sup> this is the first version with functional major gameplay elements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003293_150-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003293-150">[150]</a></sup> It is often based on the prototype created in pre-production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009244.E2.80.93245_151-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009244.E2.80.93245-151">[151]</a></sup> Alpha and first playable are sometimes used to refer to a single milestone, however large projects require first playable before <a href="/wiki/Feature_complete" title="Feature complete">feature complete</a> alpha.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003293_150-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003293-150">[150]</a></sup> First playable occurs 12 to 18 months before code release. It is sometimes referred to as the "Pre-Alpha" stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245_153-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Alpha">Alpha</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Alpha">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alpha_release" title="Alpha release">Alpha release</a></div>
<p><i>Alpha</i> is the stage when key gameplay functionality is implemented, and assets are partially finished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245_153-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245-153">[153]</a></sup> A game in alpha is <i>feature complete</i>, that is, game is playable and contains all the major features.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003192_154-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003192-154">[154]</a></sup> These features may be further revised based on testing and feedback.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245_153-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245-153">[153]</a></sup> Additional small, new features may be added, similarly planned, but unimplemented features may be dropped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003192_154-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003192-154">[154]</a></sup> Programmers focus mainly on finishing the codebase, rather than implementing additions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003294_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003294-152">[152]</a></sup> Alpha occurs eight to ten months before code release,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245_153-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245-153">[153]</a></sup> but this can vary significantly based on the scope of content and assets any given game has.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Code_freeze">Code freeze</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Code freeze">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i>Code freeze</i> is the stage when new code is no longer added to the game and only bugs are being corrected. Code freeze occurs three to four months before code release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245_153-6"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Beta">Beta</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Beta">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beta_release" title="Beta release">Beta release</a></div>
<p><i>Beta</i> is feature and asset complete version of the game, when only bugs are being fixed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003294_152-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003294-152">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245_153-7"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245-153">[153]</a></sup> This version contains no bugs that prevent the game from being shippable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003294_152-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003294-152">[152]</a></sup> No changes are made to the game features, assets, or code. Beta occurs two to three months before code release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245_153-8"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Code_release">Code release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Code release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i>Code release</i> is the stage when many bugs are fixed and game is ready to be shipped or submitted for console manufacturer review. This version is tested against QA test plan. First code release candidate is usually ready three to four weeks before code release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245_153-9"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandler2009245-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gold_master">Gold master</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Gold master">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Release_to_manufacturing" title="Release to manufacturing">Release to manufacturing</a></div>
<p><i>Gold master</i> is the final game's build that is used as a master for production of the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003295_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003295-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Crunch_time">Crunch time</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Crunch time">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Overtime" title="Overtime">Overtime</a> is expected in the games industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak2010241_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak2010241-156">[156]</a></sup> Particularly, <i>crunch time</i> or <i>crunch mode</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcShaffry200917_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcShaffry200917-157">[157]</a></sup> is unpaid overtime requested by many companies to meet project deadlines and milestones<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201020.2C_212_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201020.2C_212-158">[158]</a></sup> that negatively affects game developers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201048_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201048-159">[159]</a></sup> A team missing a deadline risks the danger of having the project cancelled<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201020_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201020-160">[160]</a></sup> or employees being laid off.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201048_159-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201048-159">[159]</a></sup> Although many companies are reducing the amount of crunch time,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak2010241_156-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak2010241-156">[156]</a></sup> it is still prominent in smaller companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201048.2C_241_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201048.2C_241-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many companies offer time-off, called <i>comp time</i> or extra <a href="/wiki/Paid_time_off" title="Paid time off">paid time off</a> after product ships to compensate for crunch time's negative effects. Some companies offer bonuses and financial rewards for successful milestone reach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak2010212_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak2010212-162">[162]</a></sup> Sometimes on-site <i>crunch meals</i> are offered and delivered to the team during crunch time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcShaffry200917_157-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcShaffry200917-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Game_Developers_Association" title="International Game Developers Association">International Game Developers Association</a> (IGDA) surveyed nearly 1,000 game developers in 2004 and produced a report to highlight the many problems caused by bad practice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-production">Post-production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Post-production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the game <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Release_to_manufacturing" title="Release to manufacturing">goes gold</a> and ships, some developers will give team members <i>comp time</i> (perhaps up to a week or two) to compensate for the overtime put in to complete the game, though this compensation is not standard.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Maintenance">Maintenance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Maintenance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Once a game ships, the maintenance phase for the video game begins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201097_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201097-164">[164]</a></sup></p>
<p>Games developed for <a href="/wiki/Video_game_console" title="Video game console">video game consoles</a> have had almost no maintenance period in the past. The shipped game would forever house as many bugs and features as when released. This was common for consoles since all consoles had identical or nearly identical hardware; making incompatibility, the cause of many bugs, a non-issue. In this case, maintenance would only occur in the case of a <a href="/wiki/Game_port" title="Game port">port</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sequel" title="Sequel">sequel</a>, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enhanced_remake" title="Enhanced remake">enhanced remake</a> that reuses a large portion of the engine and assets.</p>
<p>In recent times popularity of online console games has grown, and online capable video game consoles and online services such as <a href="/wiki/Xbox_Live" title="Xbox Live">Xbox Live</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Xbox_(console)" title="Xbox (console)">Xbox</a> have developed. Developers can maintain their software through downloadable patches. These changes would not have been possible in the past without the widespread availability of the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/IBM_PC_compatible" title="IBM PC compatible">PC</a> development is different. Game developers try to account for majority of configurations and hardware. However, the number of possible configurations of hardware and software inevitably leads to discovery of game-breaking circumstances that the programmers and testers didn't account for.</p>
<p>Programmers wait for a period to get as many bug reports as possible. Once the developer thinks they've obtained enough feedback, the programmers start working on a <a href="/wiki/Patch_(computing)" title="Patch (computing)">patch</a>. The patch may take weeks or months to develop, but it's intended to fix most accounted bugs and problems with the game that were overlooked past code release, or in rare cases, fix unintended problems caused by previous patches. Occasionally a patch may include extra features or content or may even alter gameplay.</p>
<p>In the case of a <a href="/wiki/Massively_multiplayer_online_game" title="Massively multiplayer online game">massively multiplayer online game</a> (MMOG), such as a <a href="/wiki/Massively_multiplayer_online_role-playing_game" title="Massively multiplayer online role-playing game">MMORPG</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MMORTS" title="MMORTS">MMORTS</a>, the shipment of the game is the starting phase of maintenance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201097_164-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201097-164">[164]</a></sup> Such online games are in continuous maintenance as the gameworld is continuously changed and iterated and new features are added. The maintenance staff for a popular MMOG can number in the dozens, sometimes including members of the original programming team.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Outsourcing">Outsourcing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Outsourcing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Several development disciplines, such as audio, dialogue, or motion capture, occur for relatively short periods of time. Efficient employment of these roles requires either large development house with multiple simultaneous title production or outsourcing from third-party vendors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003183_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003183-165">[165]</a></sup> Employing personnel for these tasks full-time is expensive,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003183.E2.80.93184_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003183.E2.80.93184-166">[166]</a></sup> so a majority of developers outsource a portion of the work. Outsourcing plans are conceived during the pre-production stage; where the time and finances required for outsourced work are estimated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003184_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003184-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>The music cost ranges based on length of composition, method of performance (live or synthesized), and composer experience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003343_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003343-168">[168]</a></sup> In 2003 a minute of high quality synthesized music cost between <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>600-1.5k.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003344_146-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003344-146">[146]</a></sup> A title with 20 hours of gameplay and 60 minutes of music may have cost $50k-60k for its musical score.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003345_147-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003345-147">[147]</a></sup></li>
<li>Voice acting is well-suited for outsourcing as it requires a set of specialized skills. Only large publishers employ in-house voice actors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003353_148-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003353-148">[148]</a></sup></li>
<li>Sound effects can also be outsourced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003363_144-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003363-144">[144]</a></sup></li>
<li>Programming is generally outsourced less than other disciplines, such as art or music. However, outsourcing for extra programming work or savings in salaries has become more common in recent years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke2003185_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke2003185-169">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The game production has similar distribution methods to those of music and film industries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200925_32-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200925-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>The publisher's marketing team targets the game for a specific market and then advertises it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004241_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004241-175">[175]</a></sup> The team advises the developer on target demographics and market trends,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004241_175-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004241-175">[175]</a></sup> as well as suggests specific features.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004242_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004242-176">[176]</a></sup> The game is then advertised and the game's high concept is incorporated into the promotional material, ranging from magazine ads to TV spots.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004241_175-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004241-175">[175]</a></sup> Communication between developer and marketing is important.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004242_176-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004242-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<p>The length and purpose of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_playable_demo" title="First playable demo">game demo</a> depends on the purpose of the demo and target audience. A game's demo may range between a few seconds (such as clips or screenshots) to hours of gameplay. The demo is usually intended for journalists, buyers, trade shows, general public, or internal employees (who, for example, may need to familiarize with the game to promote it). Demos are produced with public relations, marketing and sales in mind, maximizing the presentation effectiveness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004246_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004246-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trade_show_demo">Trade show demo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Trade show demo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As a game nears completion, the publisher will want to showcase a <a href="/wiki/Game_demo" title="Game demo">demo</a> of the title at trade shows. Many games have a "Trade Show demo" scheduled.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The major annual trade shows are, for example, <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Entertainment_Expo" title="Electronic Entertainment Expo">Electronic Entertainment Expo</a> (E3) or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penny_Arcade_Expo" title="Penny Arcade Expo">Penny Arcade Expo</a> (PAX).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200924.E2.80.9325_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200924.E2.80.9325-178">[178]</a></sup> E3 is the largest show in North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200357_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200357-179">[179]</a></sup> E3 is hosted primarily for marketing and business deals. New games and platforms are announced at E3 and it received broad press coverage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200924_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200924-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200358_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200358-180">[180]</a></sup> Thousands of products are on display and press demonstration schedules are kept.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethke200358_180-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethke200358-180">[180]</a></sup> In recent years E3 has become a more closed-door event and many advertisers have withdrawn, reducing E3's budget.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200924_74-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200924-74">[74]</a></sup> PAX, created by authors of <a href="/wiki/Penny_Arcade" title="Penny Arcade">Penny Arcade</a> blog and web-comic, is a mature and playful event with a player-centred philosophy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200925_32-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200925-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Localization">Localization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Localization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Video_game_localization" title="Video game localization">Video game localization</a></div>
<p>A game created in one language may also be published in other countries which speak a different language. For that region, the game needs to be translated for the game to be playable. For example, some games created for <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Vita" title="PlayStation Vita">PlayStation Vita</a> were initially published in Japanese language, like <i><a href="/wiki/Soul_Sacrifice_(video_game)" title="Soul Sacrifice (video game)">Soul Sacrifice</a></i>. Non-native speakers of the game's original language may have to wait for translation of the game to their language. But most modern big-budget games take localization into account during the development process and the games are released for several different languages simultaneously.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Localization is the actual process of translating the language assets in a game into other languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> By localizing games, they increase their level of accessibility where games could help to expend the international markets effectively. Game localization is generally known as language translations yet a "full localization" of a game is a complex project. Different levels of translation range from: zero translation being that there is no translation to the product and all things are sent raw, basic translation where only a few text and subtitles are translated or even added, and a full translation where new voice overs and game material changes are added.</p>
<p>There are various essential elements on localizing a game including translating the language of the game to adjusting in-game assets for different cultures to reach more potential consumers in other geographies (or globalization for short). Translation seems to fall into scope of localization, which itself constitutes a substantially broader endeavor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> These include the different levels of translation to the globalization of the game itself. However, certain developers seem to be divided on whether globalization falls under localization or not.</p>
<p>Moreover, in order to fit into the local markets, game production companies often change or redesign the graphic designs or the packaging of the game for marketing purposes. For example, the popular game <i><a href="/wiki/Assassin%27s_Creed" title="Assassin's Creed">Assassin's Creed</a></i> has two different packaging designs for the Japanese and US market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> By localizing the graphic and packaging designs, companies might arouse a better connections and attention from the consumers from various regions.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Indie_development">Indie development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Indie development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Independent_video_game_development" title="Independent video game development">Independent video game development</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Indie_game" title="Indie game">Independent games</a> or <i>indie games</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200927_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200927-184">[184]</a></sup> are produced by individuals and small teams with no large-scale developer or publisher affiliations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200927_184-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200927-184">[184]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak2010272_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak2010272-185">[185]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2004252_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2004252-186">[186]</a></sup> Indie developers generally rely on Internet distribution schemes. Many hobbyist indie developers create <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mod_(computer_gaming)" title="Mod (computer gaming)">mods</a> of existing games. Indie developers are credited for creative game ideas (for example, <i><a href="/wiki/Darwinia_(video_game)" title="Darwinia (video game)">Darwinia</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Weird_Worlds:_Return_to_Infinite_Space" title="Weird Worlds: Return to Infinite Space">Weird Worlds</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/World_of_Goo" title="World of Goo">World of Goo</a></i>). Current economic viability of indie development is questionable, however in recent years internet delivery platforms, such as, <a href="/wiki/Xbox_Live_Arcade" title="Xbox Live Arcade">Xbox Live Arcade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steam_(software)" title="Steam (software)">Steam</a> have improved indie game success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200927_184-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200927-184">[184]</a></sup> In fact, some indie games have become very successful, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Braid_(video_game)" title="Braid (video game)">Braid</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BraidPop_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-BraidPop-187">[187]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/World_of_Goo" title="World of Goo">World of Goo</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GooPop_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-GooPop-188">[188]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Minecraft" title="Minecraft">Minecraft</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MinePop_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-MinePop-189">[189]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_industry">Game industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Game industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Video_game_industry" title="Video game industry">Video game industry</a></div>
<p>The video game industry (formally referred to as interactive entertainment) is the economic sector involved with the development, marketing and sale of video games. The industry sports several unique approaches.</p>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-globalize" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="Globe icon." data-file-height="290" data-file-width="350" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/48px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/73px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/97px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 2x" width="48"/></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Game development <a href="/wiki/Video_game_culture" title="Video game culture">culture</a> always has been and continues to be very <a href="/wiki/Casual" title="Casual">casual</a> by normal business standards. Many game developers are strongly individualistic and usually tolerant of divergent personalities. Despite the casual culture, game development is taken seriously by its practitioners, who may take offense if it is suggested that they don't have "a real job."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Locales">Locales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Locales">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_video_game_companies" title="List of video game companies">List of video game companies</a></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, in the early history of video game development, the prominent locale for game development was the corridor from <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a> to <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a> in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201050.E2.80.9351_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201050.E2.80.9351-190">[190]</a></sup> Most new developers in the US open near such "hot beds".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201017_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201017-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>At present, many large publishers still operate there, such as: <a href="/wiki/Activision_Blizzard" title="Activision Blizzard">Activision Blizzard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capcom" title="Capcom">Capcom Entertainment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disney_Interactive" title="Disney Interactive">Disney Interactive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eidos_Interactive" title="Eidos Interactive">Eidos Interactive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foundation_9" title="Foundation 9">Foundation 9</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LucasArts_Entertainment" title="LucasArts Entertainment">LucasArts Entertainment</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Namco_Bandai_Games" title="Namco Bandai Games">Namco Bandai Games</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sega_of_America" title="Sega of America">Sega of America</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sony_Computer_Entertainment_America" title="Sony Computer Entertainment America">Sony Computer Entertainment America</a>, <a href="/wiki/THQ" title="THQ">THQ</a>. However, due to the nature of game development, many publishers are present in other regions, such as <a href="/wiki/Big_Fish_Games" title="Big Fish Games">Big Fish Games</a> (Washington), <a href="/wiki/GarageGames" title="GarageGames">GarageGames</a> (Oregon), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Majesco_Entertainment" title="Majesco Entertainment">Majesco</a> (New Jersey), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microsoft_Corporation" title="Microsoft Corporation">Microsoft Corporation</a> (Washington), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nintendo_of_America" title="Nintendo of America">Nintendo of America</a> (Washington), <a href="/wiki/Take-Two_Interactive" title="Take-Two Interactive">Take-Two Interactive</a> (New York), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SouthPeak_Interactive" title="SouthPeak Interactive">SouthPeak Interactive</a> (Virginia).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201051_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201051-191">[191]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Many universities and design schools are offering classes specifically focused on game development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201019_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak201019-12">[12]</a></sup> Some have built strategic alliances with major game development companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOxland2004309_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOxland2004309-192">[192]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak2010298_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMooreNovak2010298-193">[193]</a></sup> These alliances ensure that students have access to the latest technologies and are provided the opportunity to find jobs within the gaming industry once qualified.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Many innovative ideas are presented at conferences, such as <a href="/wiki/Independent_Games_Festival" title="Independent Games Festival">Independent Games Festival</a> (IGF) or <a href="/wiki/Game_Developers_Conference" title="Game Developers Conference">Game Developers Conference</a> (GDC).</p>
<p>Indie game development may motivate students who produce a game for their final projects or thesis and may open their own game company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200927_184-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGuireJenkins200927-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
<p>Universities offer Computer Science degrees which give you a strong basis of knowledge if you wish to become a programmer <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stability">Stability</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Video_game_development&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Stability">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Video game industry employment is fairly volatile, similar to other artistic industries including television, music, etc. Scores of game development studios crop up, work on one game, and then quickly go under.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcShaffry200919.E2.80.9320_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcShaffry200919.E2.80.9320-195">[195]</a></sup> This may be one reason why game developers tend to congregate geographically; if their current studio goes under, developers can flock to an adjacent one or start another from the ground up.</p>
<p>In an industry where only the top 20% of products make a profit,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> it's easy to understand this fluctuation. Numerous games may start development and are cancelled, or perhaps even completed but never published. Experienced game developers may work for years and yet never ship a title: such is the nature of the business. This volatility is likely inherent to the artistic nature of games.</p>

<li id="cite_note-freeman198412-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-freeman198412_62-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-freeman198412_62-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Freeman, Jon (December 1984). "Should You Turn Pro?". <i>Computer Gaming World</i>. p. 16.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AVideo+game+development&amp;rft.atitle=Should+You+Turn+Pro%3F&amp;rft.au=Freeman%2C+Jon&amp;rft.date=1984-12&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Computer+Gaming+World&amp;rft.pages=16&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span> <span class="error citation-comment" style="display:none;font-size:100%"><code style="color:inherit; border:inherit; padding:inherit;">|access-date=</code> requires <code style="color:inherit; border:inherit; padding:inherit;">|url=</code> (<a href="/wiki/Help:CS1_errors#accessdate_missing_url" title="Help:CS1 errors">help</a>)</span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Rogers-Larsen-263-63"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Rogers-Larsen-263_63-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation" id="CITEREFEverett_M._RogersJudith_K._Larsen1984">Everett M. Rogers &amp; Judith K. Larsen (1984), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=frYrAAAAYAAJ" rel="nofollow"><i>Silicon Valley fever: growth of high-technology culture</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Basic_Books" title="Basic Books">Basic Books</a>, p. 263, <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-465-07821-4" title="Special:BookSources/0-465-07821-4">0-465-07821-4</a><span class="reference-accessdate">, retrieved <span class="nowrap">2011-04-23</span></span>, <q>Video game machines have an average weekly take of $109 per machine. The video arcade industry took in $8 billion in quarters in 1982, surpassing pop music (at $4 billion in sales per year) and Hollywood films ($3 billion). Those 32 billion arcade games played translate to 143 games for every man, woman, and child in America. A recent Atari survey showed that 86 percent of the US population from 13 to 20 has played some kind of video game and an estimated 8 million US homes have video games hooked up to the television set. Sales of home video games were $3.8 billion in 1982, approximately half that of video game arcades.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AVideo+game+development&amp;rft.au=Everett+M.+Rogers&amp;rft.au=Judith+K.+Larsen&amp;rft.btitle=Silicon+Valley+fever%3A+growth+of+high-technology+culture&amp;rft.date=1984&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfrYrAAAAYAAJ&amp;rft.isbn=0-465-07821-4&amp;rft.pages=263&amp;rft.pub=Basic+Books&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
